## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed document verifier text stands where the source defines conduct gates, Phase 1 gates any fix proposal on completed investigation, Phase 4 gates any fix on a failing test case created first, fix acceptance gates on the test passing plus no other tests broken plus the issue actually resolved, and the three-strikes counter gates a fourth attempt on an architectural discussion with the human partner
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each gate converts a judgment call into a checkable precondition, has investigation happened, does a failing test exist, did the counter reach three, which is what makes the discipline enforceable rather than aspirational
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the commonest bypass is the test-after promise, I'll write the test after confirming the fix works, which the excuse table refutes, untested fixes don't stick, test first proves it

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the gates are ordered so each produces the evidence the next consumes, investigation yields the root cause the hypothesis names, the hypothesis yields the failing test, the test yields the pass-fail verdict, and the verdict feeds the strike counter, a pipeline where skipping any stage starves every later gate of its input

## Section 018: Workload Model

- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the theme's cost center is not maintenance but adoption, the discipline charges a small toll on every single incident forever, and the source's whole argument is that the toll is repaid by avoided thrashing within the same incident
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: accounting the per-incident toll without the avoided-thrash credit makes the discipline look like pure overhead, the exact framing that gets it abandoned under deadline pressure

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand beside the source's most distinctive retry doctrine, retries here govern hypotheses rather than requests, each failed fix mandates a return to Phase 1 with the new information, never a stacked second fix, the attempt counter is explicit, and the budget is three, at which point retrying stops entirely and the architecture itself goes under question with the human partner
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because fix attempts are not idempotent, each failed fix changes the system and the debugger's mental model, so the doctrine forces re-investigation between attempts and treats repeated failure as evidence about the design, not about persistence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the anti-pattern is fix stacking, don't add more fixes on top, which converts a diagnosable system into an archaeology site where the original bug hides under three partial patches
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: retry doctrine for debugging conduct, request-level retry engineering belongs to the system design theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the hypothesis-retry loop, fail, revert to investigation, single new hypothesis, single minimal test, with the three-strike stop and the architectural escalation as its backpressure valve
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the three-strikes rule is backpressure in the load-shedding sense, it detects that demand for fixes exceeds the architecture's capacity to absorb them, each fix revealing new coupling elsewhere, and sheds the load upward to a design conversation instead of letting fix attempts queue indefinitely

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed latency packet stands beside the source's performance teaching, debugging speed comes from eliminating rework rather than rushing steps, measured in its session records as fifteen flaky tests fixed with pass rates going 60 to 100 percent and the suite running 40 percent faster once guessed delays became condition polls with 10-millisecond intervals and explicit timeouts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because arbitrary sleeps set to worst-case guesses waste time on every run and still fail under load, while condition polling exits the instant the condition holds, so correctness-driven waiting is simultaneously the faster waiting
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: tightening timeouts to speed a suite without converting to conditions trades one flake population for another, the polling conversion is the fix, not braver guessing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: performance of the debugging process and its test suites, production latency budgets belong to the system design theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the two performance claims with their mechanisms, process speed via first-time fixes, suite speed via condition polling, both labeled as the source's session-reported numbers
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that both claims share one mechanism, replacing time-based guesses with evidence-based exits, the process exits investigation when the root cause is found rather than when patience runs out, and the test exits its wait when the condition holds rather than when the sleep expires, one principle expressed at two scales

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside the source's own scale limits, the discipline is written for one agent, one incident, and one hypothesis at a time, its escalation boundary is explicit, three failed fixes end individual debugging and require the human partner, and its architecture clause marks where debugging itself stops scaling, when each fix reveals new coupling elsewhere, the problem has outgrown the method
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the phases assume a single coherent investigation state, parallel hypotheses or multiple debuggers on one bug fragment the evidence chain the gates depend on, so the method scales by sequencing incidents, not by parallelizing within one
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the scale failure the source names is unbounded persistence, fix four, five, six, each locally reasonable, collectively the sheer-inertia pattern its architecture clause exists to break
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: scale limits of the debugging method, this evolution's own task splitting keeps the seed paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the three boundaries, single-hypothesis serialization, the three-strike human escalation, and the architectural horizon where fixing yields to redesign
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the architecture clause is a scale detector disguised as a stopping rule, fixes that keep surfacing new coupling are measuring the system's hidden interconnectedness, so the strike counter does double duty, bounding effort while cheaply estimating whether the codebase itself has exceeded its design's coherent scale
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to serialize hypotheses within an incident, escalate at three strikes, and read repeated cross-cutting fixes as architecture signal rather than bad luck
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the phases assume a single coherent investigation state, parallel hypotheses or multiple debuggers on one bug fragment the evidence chain the gates depend on, so the method scales by sequencing incidents, not by parallelizing within one
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the scale failure the source names is unbounded persistence, fix four, five, six, each locally reasonable, collectively the sheer-inertia pattern its architecture clause exists to break
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: scale limits of the debugging method, this evolution's own task splitting keeps the seed paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: state the three boundaries, single-hypothesis serialization, the three-strike human escalation, and the architectural horizon where fixing yields to redesign
